<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Weaving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">deriving from an obsolete <a href="/wiki/Past_participle" class="mw-redirect" title="Past participle">past participle</a> of <i>weave</i> (<a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a>, see "weft" and "weave".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Easton%27s_Bible_Dictionary_(1897)" class="mw-redirect" title="Easton&#39;s Bible Dictionary (1897)">Easton's Bible Dictionary (1897)</a> refers to numerous Biblical references to weaving:

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Weaving was an art practised in very early times (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Exodus.35:35–35:35">Ex 35:35</a>). The Egyptians were specially skilled in it (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Isaiah.19:9–19:9">Isa 19:9</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Ezekiel.27:7–27:7">Ezek 27:7</a>), and some have regarded them as its inventors.<br /><br />In the wilderness, the Hebrews practised weaving (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Exodus.26:1–26:1">Ex 26:1</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Exodus.26:8–26:8">26:8</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Exodus.28:4–28:4">28:4</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Exodus.28:39–28:39">28:39</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Leviticus.13:47–13:47">Lev 13:47</a>). It is referred to subsequently as specially the women's work (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:2_Kings.23:7–23:7">2 Kings 23:7</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Proverbs.31:13–31:13">Prov 31:13</a>, 24). No mention of the loom is found in Scripture, but we read of the "shuttle" (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Job.7:6–7:6">Job 7:6</a>), "the pin" of the beam (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Judges.16:14–16:14">Judg 16:14</a>), "the web" (13, 14), and "the beam" (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:1_Samuel.17:7–17:7">1 Sam 17:7</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:2_Samuel.21:19–21:19">2 Sam 21:19</a>). The rendering, "with pining sickness," in Isa. 38:12 (<a href="/wiki/King_James_Version_of_the_Bible" class="mw-redirect" title="King James Version of the Bible">A.V.</a>) should be, as in the <a href="/wiki/Revised_Version" title="Revised Version">Revised Version</a>, "from the loom," or, as in the margin, "from the thrum." We read also of the "warp" and "woof" (Lev. 13:48, 49, 51–53, 58, 59), but the Revised Version margin has, instead of "warp," "woven or knitted stuff."
</p></blockquote> </span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-CFF-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CFF_8-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.icac.org/delegates/sc_notices/sc_meeting_506/Cotton-From-Field-to-Fabric.pdf">"Cotton: From Field to Fabric"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.
